Public Telegram 59

Zhu Jiahua's announcement to the parents of students of Zhongshan University, relayed by Shenbao to the parents of students of National Central University: Since the East Province Incident occurred, the students of our school have occasionally abandoned their studies and rushed about calling for action. Jiahua believes that their aspirations to love the country are commendable, but sincerely believes that the way to save the country is to focus on fundamentals. Young people in school, at this time of national crisis, should be even more determined and hardworking to strengthen the basic forces for saving the country. I have repeatedly and earnestly warned them, to the point of exhaustion. Recently, they have disregarded the school's advice, and the situation has become even more tense. They have been manipulated by a few people, going on strike, holding meetings, and demonstrating, turning to attack the government, and often taking excessive actions. They have also gone to other schools to incite strikes and try to expand the movement. Within the school, they have insulted teachers and even destroyed doors and windows and beaten Professor and Secretary-General Guo, causing serious injuries and bleeding. Later, at gatherings, students were often beaten or detained, as if they were being interrogated like prisoners. School discipline has deteriorated to this point, which is truly heartbreaking. Jiahua, as the president of the school, is lacking in virtue and ability. I have failed to guide and lead them in the beginning, and I have failed to correct and remedy them later. My management has been flawed, and I cannot escape blame. I have already submitted a request to the Ministry of Education, which has been forwarded to the National Government, to resign from my position and await punishment. The matter has now escalated, shifting from external to internal, and if it is not enough internally, it is used against the school. The students are so uneasy that their actions are all abnormal. They have already voluntarily gone on indefinite strike, and the school's responsibility for teaching is impossible to fulfill. Jiahua loves the students like his own children, but today I feel helpless. I sincerely fear that if this continues, the situation will become even more unmanageable. For the safety of the students and to prevent the parents from worrying, I am sending this telegram. I hope that you, the parents, will temporarily call them back to change their environment, which will be more beneficial. I hope you will understand and forgive. Zhu Jiahua bows respectfully.

Important News

County Magistrate Wei Discusses the Fall of Xinmin 60

Jinzhou Dispatch: After the fall of the Northeast, the Liaoning Provincial Government moved to Jinzhou, governing only thirteen counties. Xinmin was the easternmost, and Japanese troops were pressing its borders. Although they hadn't overtly resorted to violent methods, it was essentially a divide between China and Japan. It was clear that the situation was precarious. However, it managed to survive for over two months, partly because the Japanese forces lacked the strength to advance westward at the time, and partly due to the effective response of the county magistrate. However, the eventual fall was undoubtedly due to the Japanese military's deliberate expansion of its occupied territory. When the county magistrate of that county, Wei, was at a moment of existential crisis, his response was firm but respectful. Even though he was temporarily under Japanese surveillance, he managed to escape from danger with the county seal, preventing the Japanese army from carrying out any schemes to falsely claim popular support. Among the officials in the Northeast, how many could fulfill their duty to protect the land like Wei? Yesterday, I visited Mr. Wei at his lodging in Jinzhou, and he described the events before and after the fall of Xinmin in great detail. I record it as follows: "Since the September 18th Incident, the arrogance of the Japanese army and its puppets has been truly lamentable. Xinmin is a small town, and local officials shouldn't make reckless statements. However, every citizen is responsible for the fate of the country. As a member of the Northeastern people, I have also offered suggestions to our leaders. I have always known that the Japanese army has ambitious plans for further expansion. After Longjiang was lost, the Japanese army gradually advanced westward. At the time, the commander of the Japanese garrison from Julu River to Xinmin was first Umeno, then changed to Takehisa, and finally Zhongshan. Their intention to occupy Xinmin was clear. Initially, they tried to lure us with benefits, and then they threatened us. I remember when the Northeast Local Maintenance Association was established, a Japanese reporter from Dalian visited me. He first asked about my position, meaning what attitude I would take towards the Central Government and the current Northeast. I said that I am an official appointed by the Central Government and only know to obey the Central Government. He then asked if I had any relationship with Yuan Jinkai and others from the Maintenance Association, and what my future intentions were. I said that the Maintenance Association is an illegal organization, and I have private friendships with Yuan and others, but they have nothing to do with official duties. The Japanese reporter then went a step further, saying, 'What would you do if Yuan and others gave you an order?' I said that since it is an illegal organization, I would certainly not accept any orders. I cannot change my position because of personal friendships. The Japanese reporter, unable to get what he wanted, then said that Zhang Xueliang and others are imposing exorbitant taxes and levies, and the people of the Northeast all want to get rid of him. What do you think? I said that Zhang is my superior, and the right to stay or go rests with the Central Government. There is no need to answer this. Then, he asked what I thought about the relationship between China and Japan. I said that this is not something I should comment on. The affairs of the country are the responsibility of others. My duty is only to maintain local peace and stability and carry out administrative affairs. Finally, he asked if I could maintain the security of this area, and whether I was afraid that the bandits here would be unfavorable to me, and whether it would be better to ask the Japanese army to protect me. I said that my presence here is precisely to protect the local area and foreigners, and I believe I still have this ability. The reporter left disappointed. In my opinion, he must have been a Japanese spy, used to probe the intentions of our officials and people. Later, the Japanese consul also occasionally revealed intentions of enticement, but I was never moved. Soon, the Japanese army benefited from places like Longjiang and actively advanced westward. At the same time, Xinmin itself had Japanese troops, and our troops were also stationed in the Jindong area. Historically, there have been many bandits outside the Guan, and due to the confrontation between the two armies, bandits gathered in the county, and the county of hundreds of miles accumulated 5,000 bandits, while the Xinmin County Government only had more than 200 public security team members. Thanks to my many efforts, it was not ravaged. Later, the Japanese army, through Ronin, recruited four bandit groups: Binzi, Lezi, Dingzi, and Beihai, and gathered them around Jixiangbao, intending to take action. Residents reported this, saying that the bandits were wearing white armbands, with the words 'National Self-Defense Army' printed on them, and a five-color red star in the middle, clearly no different from the Japanese flag. After hearing this, I immediately visited the Japanese consul and protested. The Japanese consul strongly denied it. By the 19th, rumors spread that the pacified bandits were about to attack the city. Merchants panicked and came to the office to persuade me to abandon the city. I solemnly declared that if the Japanese army attacked the city, I would definitely leave, because the Central Government had long ordered not to take hostile actions against the Japanese army. However, if bandits harass, I, as the head of a county, cannot leave my post without authorization and must maintain it to the end. On the evening of the 20th, the situation became even more tense. At 2:00 AM, I and my colleagues in the county office were taking turns on duty when we received a report that a guard at the gate near the county office discovered a group of people placing two heavy objects on the ground and secretly lighting them. The guard shot at them, but missed. Upon closer inspection, they were rice straws coated with lard, one end lit and the other end attached to two bombs. It was certain that the form and source of the straws must be Korean. At that time, they were burning very quickly, and the guards hurriedly retreated. Residents, upon hearing the news, did not dare to approach. Knowing that there would be a major event that night, I immediately telegraphed the city's public security bureau to tighten defenses. Soon, gunshots were heard at the east gate, and the bandits launched a large-scale attack on the city. At the same time, the burning straw, blown by the wind, separated from the bombs, fortunately without exploding. It was then carried into the office. On one hand, the police tried their best to resist the bandits. At dawn, the bandits were repelled. I then went to the Japanese consulate, and found that there were also two similar bombs in the consulate's courtyard. There was no doubt that they had been placed by the Japanese themselves. When the Japanese consul met me, he pretended to be surprised, saying he didn't know where these two strange things came from. I told him that similar things had been found near the county office, and that their form was definitely not something that could be found in Xinmin. Then, I solemnly warned the Japanese consul, saying that if your country wants to occupy Xinmin, I can only retreat, because I have repeatedly received orders not to take hostile actions against your army. Your army's use of bandits seems too clumsy, and it is an overreaction. Occupying Xinmin does not require such measures. At that time, the Japanese consul still tried to argue. At 6:00 AM that day, he even accompanied me to inspect various places. As a result, it was discovered that three places in the city had been bombed, two houses had been burned, and a large basket of bullet casings had been collected. Fortunately, the attack locations had not hit any important points. The Japanese consul's attitude seemed to regret that his Japanese bullets had been wasted on empty targets, as if this action had not achieved its intended goal. At 10:00 AM, Commander Zhongshan came to Xinmin again and met me with a artillery captain. He immediately began to speak wildly, reaching the extreme of rudeness, saying that he could not guarantee the safety of the Japanese consul, and that someone had secretly placed a bomb in the consulate, for which I must take full responsibility. I told him that this object was not only not from Xinmin, but also unknown to the people of Xinmin, and that since the September 18th Incident, I had forbidden people from passing near the consulate, and the consulate itself was heavily guarded, so how could the bomb have entered? Although the commander had no words to answer, he still babbled on incessantly. Afterwards, the translator told me that he was actually cursing me, hating that I didn't understand Japanese, and that the interpreter was afraid that I would clash with the Japanese, so he didn't tell me the truth at the time, otherwise I would never have allowed him to be so rude. After they left, the Japanese army intermittently shelled westward from Julu River. Also, before the bandits took action, there would always be Japanese artillery fire, so there was no doubt that there was an agreement between them. On the afternoon of the 21st, at 4:00 PM, the bandits launched another attack, which was also repelled. On the 22nd, I learned that the bandits had gathered at Gaotaizi. I notified the Japanese consul, saying that I would send people to suppress the bandits there, but that area was very close to your army's defense line, and I was afraid of causing misunderstandings, so I came to inform you. The Japanese consul initially had no objection. I then dispatched 120 cavalrymen from the self-defense corps, led by Wang Xiaozhong, to that area. Unexpectedly, the Japanese army opened fire, killing or wounding more than 30 people from our side on the spot. On the evening of the 24th, the Japanese side then sent troops themselves. After entering the city, a Japanese man, together with bandit leader Jin Zehui, led the so-called self-defense army straight to the county office. I happened to be coming from outside and planned to temporarily take refuge in a nearby store, but I was suddenly spotted by several directors of the county chamber of commerce, who pleaded with me to go to the chamber of commerce, saying that the Japanese were looking for the county magistrate to discuss post-settlement measures. Reluctantly, I went with them to the chamber of commerce. The Japanese then proposed two conditions: first, I had to sign a statement declaring that I would be subject to the control of the puppet government of Shenyang; second, I had to issue a document proving that I welcomed the Japanese army. In his words, he also presented a proclamation by Honjo, which had been drafted in advance, the general idea of which was that 'this army has come at the request of all sectors of Xinmin,' etc. These documents were forced upon me and the president of the chamber of commerce to co-sign. The people of the chamber of commerce all spoke for the sake of the safety of Xinmin, asking me to sign. I then told them that it was my responsibility to maintain the ground, and if I could no longer maintain it, then I could only allow the Japanese army to do what they wanted, but I am a national official, and you should persuade me to love my country, not to tempt me to betray my country. I would swear to deny the signing. Seeing that my will was unyielding, the local people made a temporary maintenance association stamp, posted a proclamation to pacify the people. I was detained in the Japanese consulate until 3:00 AM before being released, but they then sent four military police and one soldier to secretly monitor me. I pretended to be ill and stayed at the Xinhuo Inn near the county office, while the Japanese soldiers guarded outside. From the 24th to the 25th, on the 26th, a phone call came from Shenyang, saying that an appointment would be sent. I responded casually. When a conflict occurred in the front, the Japanese army rushed to the front line, and I was able to take the opportunity to escape. I also secretly brought the seal to avoid the creation of false evidence to confuse international opinion. I then took a horse from Mincun, passed through Niujia Wopeng, and boarded a train at Xinli Town to Jinzhou. However, because I had not ridden a horse for many years and had not been able to rest, I felt very tired. After arriving in Jinzhou, I visited the Chief of Staff and received great comfort, which made me feel even more ashamed. The current situation in that area is not yet fully clear, but I have one very important statement to make, which is that the Japanese army is forcibly distorting public opinion with all kinds of false evidence, proclaiming to the world that wherever the Japanese army goes, they are welcomed by the Chinese. If foreigners do not understand the truth, they will inevitably reverse right and wrong. If the Japanese treat Xinmin like this, who knows if they will treat other counties in Liaodong the same way? The impact of this is very great. This point must be made clear to the world, otherwise it will be very detrimental to our side."

Shenyang to Become Japanese Administrative Center 61

Kwantung Army Headquarters to Permanently Station in Shenyang; South Manchuria Railway Company Also to Move from Dalian to Shenyang. The World News Agency reports, citing Japanese sources, that since the Manchurian Incident, all important Japanese agencies in Manchuria have actually moved to Shenyang. It is now heard that the South Manchuria Railway Company will also move from Dalian to Shenyang soon. This issue has been decided after discussions between the South Manchuria Railway Company President Uchida and other key members with relevant authorities. The location for setting up the agency has already been selected, and negotiations for purchasing the land have begun. It is also rumored that the Kwantung Army Headquarters has tentatively decided to permanently station in Shenyang, and the transfer of its various teams and agencies is being planned. Currently, the management of the South Manchuria Railway area is distributed among the Kwantung Army, the Kwantung Government, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Tokyo. Now, it is planned to give all authority to the President of the South Manchuria Railway Company to achieve unification. It is expected that Shenyang will soon become the center of Japanese administrative and other activities.

Fuzhou Electric Company Refuses Inspection, Sparking Anti-Japanese Tide 62

Inciting Workers to Beat Up Anti-Japanese Association Members

All Sectors Halt Business, Demanding Government Punishment

Fuzhou Correspondence: The Disciplinary Committee of the Anti-Japanese Association of all circles in the provincial capital, because the Fuzhou Electric Company (organized by the Liu brothers, including the directors and managers of the Electric Company), used the Liu Zhengji's (i.e. organized by the Liu family brothers who are the directors and managers of the Electric Company) Xin Jian and Xin Sheng ships to travel back and forth between Taiwan and Dalian, purchasing and transporting large quantities of coal, foreign cement, raw oil, and various electrical materials to Fujian for sale, repeatedly warned them without effect, and resolved to punish the company with 30,000 yuan and confiscate all the goods. At 2:00 PM on the 3rd of this month, Anti-Japanese Association member Chen Xuehua and Disciplinary Committee member Lin Pingzhou led more than 20 inspectors, taking a public bus to the Xinguang Electric Company to seal up the items. The company's secretary, Lin Xianmin, met them and led them into the upstairs living room. While they were negotiating, more than 100 workers suddenly gathered downstairs, making a lot of noise, saying that the Anti-Japanese Association members should leave immediately, or they would be beaten to death. As the members were about to persuade them, the workers suddenly rushed up and started hitting them, and the entire group was trapped in the living room. The driver of the car waiting outside the door saw the situation was not good and quickly drove to the Anti-Japanese Association to report. The Anti-Japanese Association then reported to the Provincial and County Party Headquarters. The Provincial Party Headquarters sent Director Liu Chengqing, and the County Party Headquarters sent member Cheng Jiakai, along with the Martial Law Headquarters' Inspection Team and the City Public Security Bureau's Detective Team to the scene. They first dispersed the workers, then released the Anti-Japanese Association members, and asked the company's secretary, Lin Xianmin, why they had beaten up the Anti-Japanese Association members. Lin claimed that the workers had acted on their own and had nothing to do with the company, and that the company usually had bad feelings with various circles because of inspections for stealing electricity, and was afraid that bad people would take the opportunity to cause trouble, and requested the dispatch of soldiers and police for protection. After this incident, the public was indignant at the company for inciting workers to brutally beat up Anti-Japanese Association members and undermine the national salvation movement, and there was a great tendency to attack it en masse. The Party and government authorities, seeing the intense anger of the people and fearing that it would cause a major disturbance, held a joint meeting of the Provincial Party Headquarters and the Provincial Government at 10:00 AM on the 4th, deciding to first investigate the truth of the matter, and then sent Provincial Party Headquarters members Gan Yun and Wang Huaijin, and Provincial Government members Cheng Shikui and Xu Xianshi to the company to check whether the imported goods were Japanese products before proceeding further. At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, various groups also held an emergency meeting at the County Party Headquarters, attended by more than 200 representatives, and resolved six items: (1) request the Provincial Government to arrest Liu Chongwei and Liu Chonglun and hand them over to all circles for public trial; (2) confiscate all the property of Liu Zhengji's warehouse and company to cover the expenses of Ma Zhanshan's army; (3) take back the electric company for official or municipal operation; (4) arrest the thugs Lin Tianmin, Lin Xianmin, Shi Jingchao, Zheng Yanguang, etc. and punish them according to law; (5) all Japanese goods seized by the electric company should be confiscated; (6) the electric company should compensate the victims for medical expenses. After the meeting, all the representatives went to the Provincial Government to petition for implementation, and were met by members Chen Peikun and Zheng Baojing, and Secretary-General Chen Shoufan. In response to the conditions proposed by the representatives, they promised to wait for the Party and government members to investigate and return to see what the situation was before proceeding according to law. The representatives, fearing that Lin Tianmin, Lin Xianmin, and others would flee beforehand, requested that the police be immediately dispatched to arrest them pending further action. Members Chen and Zheng agreed. The representatives then went to the County Party Headquarters to continue the meeting, deciding that if the authorities did not have a satisfactory solution, a city-wide strike would be held on the 5th to express their determination, leaving representatives from the Anti-Japanese Association of all circles: students, merchants, workers, and four groups to wait for a reply, and the rest temporarily dispersed. At around 7:00 PM in the evening, the Party and government members completed their investigation. The four representatives went to the Provincial Party Headquarters to inquire. They were told that more than 2,000 bags of foreign cement were indeed products of the Asano Company, and more than 600 boxes of soybean oil had the Taisho era year printed on the boxes. The remaining coal and electrical materials were also identified as mostly Japanese goods. The electric company stated that they were all handled before the boycott, but it was also inappropriate not to register with the Anti-Japanese Association, and they were advised to tell all circles to wait quietly for the government to deal with it, and not to act rashly. However, because the representatives believed that the authorities had not yet given a concrete answer to the conditions proposed by the assembly, the entire city had implemented a strike on the 5th, with shops closing their doors and students suspending classes. The Provincial Government is scheduled to hold another joint meeting of the Party and government on the afternoon of the 5th to discuss solutions (December 5th).

The 48th Executive Yuan National Affairs Conference 63

The Executive Yuan held its 48th National Affairs Conference on the morning of the 8th. Those present were Song Ziwen, Liu Ruiheng, Ma Fuxiang, Wang Boqun, and Li Shuhua. Those attending were Shi Ci, Zhao Xien, Hai Ci Chen Shaokuan, Military Ci Chen Yi, Railway Ci Qian Zongze, Nei Ci Zhang Wuhua, Secretary-General Lu Bichou, and Political Affairs Director Xu Jingzhi. Song Ziwen chaired the meeting. The matters discussed were as follows: (1) The Department of Industry, Commerce, and Agriculture submitted a case for review and approval regarding the conversion of reclaimed land back to lakes and the commencement of Huai River management starting with its outlet to the sea to prevent flooding. The three departments dispatched personnel and convened experts and representatives of relevant agencies to jointly discuss the matter. Regarding the conversion of reclaimed land back to lakes, two principles and five proposed measures were agreed upon. Regarding the commencement of Huai River management starting with its outlet to the sea, due to differing opinions among the experts and representatives, it was resolved to request those who advocated for first managing the river's inlet and those who advocated for first managing its outlet to the sea to submit separate written opinions for review and approval by the ministry and then the Executive Yuan for selection and implementation. Aside from the Huai River issue, which will be submitted separately for review, the agreed-upon measures for the conversion of reclaimed land back to lakes are submitted first for review and implementation. It was resolved to approve the measures after review by the three departments. (2) The Department of Industry submitted a draft of the Factory Registration Regulations for review and record. It was resolved to approve the record. (3) It was resolved to approve the resignation of Li Zhonggong, member of the Anhui Provincial Government and Director of the Department of Education, and request approval for He Qigong, a member of the committee, to concurrently serve as Director of the Department of Education. Also, Yu Enbo, a member of the committee and Acting Director of the Department of Education, requested approval to be relieved of his concurrent position. Also, Hao Guoxi, a member of the committee, resigned, and it was requested that Fan Xiji be appointed to succeed him. (4) It was resolved to approve the request of Huang Shiheng, member of the Hunan Provincial Government and Director of the Department of Education, to resign from his concurrent position as Director of the Department of Education, and request that Cao Dianqiu, a member of the committee, be appointed to concurrently serve in that position. (5) It was resolved to appoint Qi Qi as the Lieutenant Colonel Section Chief of the Pensions and Awards Section of the Military Assessment Department of the Army Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs, and Wen Yanbin as the Lieutenant Colonel Section Chief of the Inspection Section of the Ordnance Department of the Army Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs. (6) It was resolved that the Director of the Gong County Arsenal, Lu Mingui, and the Deputy Director of the Shanghai Arsenal, Zhang Chunpu, both under the Department of Ordnance of the Ministry of Military Affairs, would be appointed to other positions. Also, Huang Gongzhu, Director of the Jinling Arsenal, would be appointed to another position, and it was requested that they be relieved of their duties. It was also requested that Wu Kerun be appointed as the Director of the Gong County Arsenal, Huang Shang as the Director of the Jinan Arsenal, Liu Chucun as the Director of the Huayin Arsenal, and Yang Jizeng as the Deputy Director of the Shanghai Arsenal. (7) It was resolved that Zhao Zhiyou, Director of the Bureau of Public Works of the Nanjing Municipal Government, would be appointed to another position. Water Patrol Team Captures Bandit, Sends Him to County for Interrogation The Water Patrol Team of this county, which was just established at the beginning of the month, had its patrol officer, Fei Gongxia, capture a bandit named Liu Asan at the Shihudang train station. Wuxi 66

Road Construction Funds Completely Depleted Construction Bureau Director Yao Dixing recently received a telegram from the Provincial Department ordering him to remit 15,288 yuan of road construction Cai Jin to the Provincial Treasury. After receiving the order, Director Yao immediately sent an official letter to the Bank of Communications to inform them. After the bank approved the letter, it stated that the road construction Mu tax had already been used for dike repair and disaster relief, and that the Disaster Relief Committee had previously informed them that the funds could not be used without the committee's notification. However, the Construction Bureau repeatedly requested the bank to withdraw the funds, but the bank politely refused. However, according to the Business Tax Regulations, it was difficult to refuse again, so yesterday it specifically sent a letter to the Disaster Relief Committee to inquire. After receiving the letter, the committee immediately submitted it to the 10th cadre director's standing committee for discussion and resolution. It was still decided that the Provincial Department and the County Government Construction Bureau should be notified that the previous transfer of road construction Mu tax to dike repair and disaster relief should be insisted upon, and that 50,000 yuan of silver should be allocated from the construction expenses. If this request was not granted, it would mean that the government was indifferent to the people's hardships and only knew how to collect taxes from the people, without any practical determination for water conservancy construction. In the future, if there were disasters, they should bear full responsibility, and the committee would announce its dissolution. At the same time, Zou Tongyi, Director of General Affairs of the committee, upon hearing that the funds had been completely withdrawn by Director Yao, felt that there were no funds for dike repair in the future, so he refused to meet with such people who did not care about the local area at the meeting place, and also sent a letter to the Disaster Relief Committee yesterday requesting approval for his resignation. Three Robbers Arrested on the Spot The home of farmer Ni Xiaochun in Anzhen Jiaoshan Shima Bay, Eighth District (Huai Xia Shi), was suddenly visited by three robbers at about 10:00 PM on the 5th of this month. They climbed over the wall and entered, robbing at will. As a result, 19 pieces of clothing and 2 quilts were taken. At that time, Meng Guangyou, the squad leader of the Dongting Town Security Regiment, happened to be leading his soldiers on patrol near the Xintang Bridge when he saw three people carrying packages, looking flustered. He immediately arrested them all and took them back for interrogation. According to their confession, Wang Dabao, Xu Xiaomeng, and Xu Sanhe all admitted to robbing Ni Xiaochun's home. They were then sent to the county government for questioning yesterday. At 4:00 PM, Chief Wang opened the court for interrogation. Later, the plaintiff Ni Xiaochun was summoned to court to identify them, and it was confirmed that they were the robbers. The three robbers were then nailed, chained, and taken into custody to await investigation.

Discovery of 2,000 Ounces of Opium at Zhakou Station Yesterday, when a freight train from Shanghai arrived at Zhakou Station in Hangzhou, two passengers, Jiang Yanding and Zhao Hanqing, forged a pass from a certain military headquarters to avoid inspection. They transported over 2,000 ounces of opium and over 900 bags of red pills from Shanghai. After getting off the train, they hired porters to carry them onto the ship. The goods were packed in three large rattan suitcases. The inspectors from the Fourth District suspected that their luggage was heavy and ordered them to be inspected. The large batch of opium and red pills was discovered. The two criminals were arrested and interrogated. Due to the seriousness of the case, they were immediately sent to the Hangzhou District Court for detention and interrogation.

He has a residence in Ningbo, on the north shore of Hefeng Doutou, with three buildings and five huts. Bengbu 72

Inspection of Japanese Goods Causes Uproar: After the establishment of the All Circles Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association in this area, due to the abundance of Japanese goods in Bengbu City, in order to thoroughly ban them, members have been dispatched to various businesses and shops for inspection in recent days. Yesterday, it was reported that Tianxiang Store, which sells Beijing-Guangdong goods on Dama Road, had a large stock of Japanese goods, which were not fully registered, displayed, and sold. The association then sent inspectors Wang Ruobo and others to the store for inspection at 3:00 PM. The store refused the inspection, leading to verbal conflict. Several store employees took off their clothes and surrounded Wang and others, acting aggressively, intending to assault them. Fortunately, someone surnamed Lu and a police officer from the post intervened and persuaded them, preventing any disaster. The inspectors reported back to the association. The Anti-Japanese Association considered the unscrupulous merchants to be refusing inspection of Japanese goods and intending to commit assault, and believed they should be severely punished. They held a meeting at 3:00 PM on the fourth day of the month to discuss countermeasures. At 7:00 PM in the evening, all inspectors of the Anti-Japanese Association, together with soldiers from the Military Police Inspectorate and police officers from the Public Security Bureau, went to Tianxiang for a second review. They seized dozens of pieces of Japanese goods such as velvet blankets and leather balls, which were sealed up for disposal. It is heard that the store has hired someone to intercede with the Anti-Japanese Association for lenient treatment, but it is unknown whether it will be approved.

Education News

Special Report: Necessary Improvements to Educational Facilities in Elementary and Secondary Schools in the Face of Brutal Japan's Active Aggression (Part 1) (Wu Zengjie) 73

Recently, brutal Japan has been advancing steadily. Liaoning and Jilin are no longer our recovered lands, and Heilongjiang Province has also been lost. Which people in the country are not heartbroken? We are in this serious situation and feel that we must strive to become strong and cannot delay any longer. The work of striving to become strong depends on all the people of our country to take on. The responsibility of our colleagues in the education sector is even greater, because those who are educated are either young people or children. Young people are the pillars of the country, and children are the masters of the future. Without healthy and complete children, how can there be healthy and complete young people? Without promising young people, the country will lose its vitality. Therefore, elementary school education is the foundation of all education. The responsibility of colleagues who serve elementary school education can be said to be the most onerous.

In this situation, what kind of policy should we adopt for the education of children, and how should we improve the facilities? It is worthy of research. Can elementary school students resist foreign aggression? Can they do practical national salvation work? Of course not, because in childhood, knowledge is insufficient and ability is lacking. We cannot ask children to do national salvation work immediately. What we must do practically for children is to "make children physically strong, cultivate the habit of using their hands and brains, and the spirit of enduring hardship, and cultivate strength to lay the foundation for national salvation in the future." Does a child simply knowing the fact that Japan has invaded the three northeastern provinces mean they can save the country? No. Does listening to a teacher's lecture on how to save the country mean they can save the country? No. If children are to be able to truly do national salvation work in the future, they must cultivate the strength to save the country.

Since Japan invaded the three northeastern provinces, the teaching in general elementary schools has centered on this event, connecting the teaching materials of various subjects and often talking to elementary school students about anti-Japanese methods and portraying the situation of Japanese atrocities. This work is certainly very good, but it is only biased towards knowledge. We must know that it is relatively easy to make elementary school students understand the atrocities of Japan, but if we only let elementary school students know without cultivating strength, then so-called national salvation is really just empty talk.

Youth Volunteer Army Training Office Issues Organizational Guidelines 77

Wang Boling, Training Supervisor of the Shanghai Student Volunteer Army Training Office, is striving to improve the Student Volunteer Army in various schools in this city. For the sake of unifying the organization, he has issued the "Organizational Guidelines for the Shanghai Student Volunteer Army" and ordered all schools to implement it according to the organization's structure. The articles are recorded below: A. General Rules: (1) After the implementation of this organization, all military training institutions in each school will be reorganized and implemented according to the organizational regulations. (2) After the implementation of this organization, the Military Training Department of the Student Federation will be abolished. All personnel must participate in the military training organization of this office and each school and be determined by this office's assessment. (3) Shanghai student military training is an independent subject. Its organizational system is completely under the direct jurisdiction of this office, which is fully responsible for training. (4) Each school is an organizational unit, and the union of each school is the organizational structure of the entire volunteer army. Within the volunteer army system, each school is a unit of a certain rank. (5) The military training instructors hired by each school must be assessed by this office and submitted to the Training Supervisor Department for approval before they can formally become military training instructors and be subject to the command of this office in military training. (6) In order to ensure the integrity of the school's administrative power, a political department may be set up within the highest military organization stage of each school, filled by the principal, dean of academic affairs, and training personnel. (7) In order to ensure the completeness of the overall military training, a staff group may be set up within the highest military organization stage of each school, filled by the military instructors and sports personnel of each school, to make an overall military training plan and be responsible for its implementation. (8) In order to ensure the tension and integrity of the school's military training, each school will set up a disciplinary committee, staffed by school training personnel and no more than ten students. B. Organization: (9) The head of the highest military unit in each school will be the best instructor. (10) The squad leader and deputy squad leader will be the best students. (11) The platoon leader and above will be instructors and sports personnel. (12) Students may be appointed as platoon leaders when necessary. (13) Each school must, according to the organization chart, select students from each grade, except those selected as squad leaders and deputy squad leaders, and assign the names of the students to each class. (14) The assignment of students will be completed by the school's training director in cooperation with the military instructor within a short period of time. (15) The officers in charge of the organization will be determined separately by this office. (16) As soon as the new organization of each school is ready, the old organization will be abolished, and after formally appointing the officers and squad leaders at all levels, an oath ceremony will be held, which will be the completion of the organization. C. Outline of the powers of each group: (17) The officers in charge of the highest unit within the volunteer army organization of each school are responsible for the following for the troops under their jurisdiction: 1. Military discipline responsibility; 2. Training responsibility; 3. Command (during training exercises) responsibility. (18) The military instructor of the volunteer army in each school is responsible for the following: 1. Under the guidance of the senior officers, take responsibility for training; 2. The command responsibility of serving as an officer in the organization. (19) The responsibilities of the Political Department are as follows: 1. The right to request administrative matters related to military training; 2. The responsibility to assist military training to facilitate its speedy completion; 3. Implement the resolutions of the Disciplinary Committee. (20) The responsibilities of the Staff Group are as follows: 1. Research and decide on the military training plan; 2. Assist the chief military officer in military training and its implementation; 3. Contribute suggestions for improving military training. (21) The responsibilities of the Disciplinary Committee are: 1. Assist the volunteer army officers to achieve the purpose of training; 2. Tighten the momentum of the students; 3. Decide on the punishment items for students. (22) The detailed rules for the political department, the staff group, the disciplinary committee, and the volunteer army officers will be determined separately.

Office Set Up in Minli Middle School

County Education Funding Audit Committee Held Regular Meeting Yesterday 81

The Shanghai County Education Bureau held the first regular meeting of the Funding Audit Committee yesterday afternoon. The attendees were Yu Yanfen, Dai Zuyi, Sun Jichu, Zhang Yinghao, Zhong Youde, Yang Huiming, Zheng Guozhai, Peng Liren, Zhang Yi, and Jin Zuobin. Yu Yanfen chaired the meeting. The ceremony was performed, and the establishment meeting and resolutions of the previous session were reported. The following discussion was then held: (1) How should the audit method be stipulated? The following resolutions were made: (A) In terms of income, review whether the income classification book, the monthly final account book, and the income and expenditure comparison table are consistent with each other. As for whether the monthly income is in line with the budget, it will not be reviewed for the time being due to the inability to calculate the average. (B) In terms of expenditure, attention should be paid to ensuring that the regular and temporary doors of expenditure do not exceed the budget. For the temporary doors, the expenditure should be as much as possible depending on the amount that should be spent on each item. (2) How should this session review the expenses for September and October and form groups to recommend personnel for review? It was resolved to recommend Jin Zuobin, Zhong Youde, Zhang Fengshan, and Peng Liren to review the expenses for September, and Yu Yanfen, Dai Zuyi, Zhang Yinghao, and Sun Jichu to review the expenses for October. Audit comments: (1) Due to the allocation of numbers in the first and second districts of the compulsory education expenditure section, which is inconsistent with the audit points, the audit is temporarily postponed. (2) In the future, the current monthly recurring expenses should be listed in the calculation book for the current month as a principle to ensure compliance with the budget. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Completion of the World Swimming Pool in Los Angeles, USA 92

The World Games, to be held in Los Angeles, USA next July, will use the city's existing municipal stadium as the venue, and its reconstruction project has long been completed. However, the swimming pool, which is an additional facility, is located to the north of the athletic field. Construction officially began on August 5 of this year and took three months, and it was completed at the end of November. Its equipment is the most magnificent and spacious in the world. The spectator stands are made of reinforced concrete and can accommodate 100,000 spectators. The pool is 50 meters long and 20 meters wide, with a maximum depth of 5 meters and a minimum depth of 1.5 meters. The water is supplied directly from the Los Angeles water source, and it is equipped with the latest filters and purifiers, which are superior to the swimming pools of previous games.

Sun Ke and Others Left Hong Kong for Shanghai Yesterday 94

Arrival Expected Tomorrow Afternoon or the Morning After

Li Shizeng Ordered to Shanghai for Long Talk with Wang

Shanghai's Central Committee Members to be Dealt with by the Fourth Plenary Session

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, Li Shizeng, the representative from Beijing, was ordered to Shanghai the day before yesterday afternoon. Yesterday afternoon around 4:00 PM, he had a long conversation with Wang Jingwei, the representative from Guangdong. The content of the conversation is unknown. Furthermore, after the closing of the Fourth Plenary Session of Guangdong, four representatives, Sun Ke, Wu Chaochu, Li Wenfan, and Chen Youren, were appointed and left Hong Kong for Shanghai yesterday. They are expected to arrive in Shanghai around tomorrow afternoon or the morning after. They will then meet with representatives from Beijing to discuss the opening of the First Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Committee. As for the ten Central Committee members elected in Shanghai, according to Wang Jingwei, they will be dealt with by the Fourth Plenary Session. The details of each piece of news are as follows:

Wang and Li's Long Talk

Around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, Beijing sent representative Li Shizeng to Shanghai. Yesterday afternoon, Wang wrote to Li, inviting him to meet at Chu Minyi's residence on Avenue Albert. Wang arrived at Chu's residence around 2:00 PM with his wife, Chen Bijun, and others, waiting for Li. Li arrived around 4:00 PM. The two met for about one and a half hours, with Chu also present to listen. Li left around 6:30 PM. Afterwards, when reporters inquired with Wang, Wang said that the meeting with Li was just a chat and there was no discussion of anything substantive. Reporters inquired elsewhere but also did not get any definite information. The content of the conversation is currently unknown.

Sun and Others Arrive in Shanghai

After the closing of the Fourth Plenary Session of Guangdong, Sun Ke, Wu Chaochu, Li Wenfan, and Chen Youren were appointed to come to Shanghai for discussions. Sun and the others were originally scheduled to leave Hong Kong the day before yesterday (the 7th), but later, due to the urgency of the matter, it was changed to yesterday. According to Guangdong representative Wang Jingwei, he has received a report from Guangdong stating that Guangdong has sent Sun, Wu, Li, and Chen as representatives, who are traveling to Shanghai on the President Coolidge of the Dollar Steamship Line, expected to arrive here around tomorrow. Furthermore, according to Madam Sun Zhesheng, Sun will arrive in Shanghai by plane, expected to arrive in the next day or two. It is not known which is correct.

The Issue of the Ten Committee Members

Regarding the issue of the ten committee members elected by the Guangdong representatives who walked out of the meeting at the Fourth Plenary Session of Guangdong and held a meeting in Shanghai some days ago, according to Wang, this matter is not a major problem. Currently, Guangdong has not officially recognized the twenty-four new committee members elected by Beijing, and Beijing has not officially recognized the twenty-four new committee members elected by Guangdong. (According to the reporter, the resolution of the peace conference stipulated that the new committee members elected by both sides must be mutually recognized.) Therefore, the issue of these ten committee members can be decided by the First Plenary Session of the Fourth Executive and Supervisory Committees, so as not to cause any disputes. The various rumors circulating outside are not credible.

Zou Lu Issues Statement 95

Guangdong representative Zou Lu stated to a Far Eastern News Agency reporter yesterday that it is regrettable that the new diplomatic policy of the Nanjing government is insincere. Dr. Wellington Koo's proposal to establish a buffer zone in the northeast of Jinzhou is a major error. It raises the suspicion that Koo's action is simply to cede Manchuria to the Japanese. The Nanjing government, due to the opposition of the national public to its new diplomatic policy, has suddenly gone back on its word and denied having this proposition. This is not only unfaithful to the people of the country, but also leaves people in the community unaware of the government's true diplomatic policy intentions. The student and public movements are entirely driven by patriotism, and Nanjing's attempt to suppress the people's patriotic movement will only increase the people's resentment towards the government. Nanjing's detention of students, the shooting of seven students in Changsha, and the strict prohibition of railway staff from transporting students to Nanjing to petition all serve to increase the stimulation of the Chinese people and youth and cause them to lose faith in the government.

Youth Support-Manchuria Corps Postpones Departure to Tomorrow Morning 96

Preparations Before and After Departure

According to Guowen News Agency, the Youth Volunteer Corps to Support Manchuria and Resist Japan has already received the understanding of the Central Government, which ordered the railway bureau to prepare first-class carriages for them. However, the corps intends not to accept them and will still march to Beijing, and has postponed the departure by one day. The news of yesterday is as follows:

Corps Members' Race

The corps believes that the work on this journey is arduous and cannot be forcibly undertaken by those with weak endowments and unhealthy bodies. Therefore, at 2:00 PM yesterday, the corps members engaged in a race in the suburbs of Zhenru for four hours to weed out those who could not undertake long-distance walking, so as to avoid feeling stuck and unable to move forward or backward midway.

Railway Bureau Prepares Carriages

Yesterday, after the Central Government ascertained that the corps members were purely patriotic individuals, driven by patriotic enthusiasm, without any partisan agenda, it was deemed possible to provide assistance. Therefore, not only did it not hinder their journey, but it also issued orders to military police in various places to provide protection. The Ministry of Railways also ordered the railway bureau to prepare first-class carriages for them. However, the corps' spirit is driven by resisting Japan and saving the country, and they have long disregarded issues of honor and disgrace. Therefore, they unanimously stated that they must adhere to their original intention and still march to Beijing.

Postponement of Departure

The corps was originally scheduled to depart from Zhenru this morning, but yesterday they temporarily postponed it by one day and are now scheduled to march to Beijing at dawn tomorrow.

Corps Meeting

Because the original members of each group have mostly left the corps, and many new members have joined, the corps held a corps meeting at Jinan University yesterday in order to strengthen the internal organization, re-allocated organizational duties, and assigned each new member to serve in each department according to their abilities, so that talents could be used and people could be used effectively.

Donations from All Circles

Minister of Military and Political Affairs He Yingqin specially donated 500 yuan in living expenses to the corps yesterday. Shanghai Mayor Zhang Qun and Public Security Bureau Chief Chen Xizeng each donated 100 yuan to the corps for travel expenses. In addition, Mr. Wang Dafo came to Jinan University to send clothing and expressed his bitterness at not being able to go north with them. Seeing the loyalty and courage of each corps member, and being prevented from going north immediately by the railway bureau, he shed tears for two hours. He was so deeply affected that he fainted on the spot and was resuscitated and sent back by the corps members.

Telegram to Zhang Xueliang

Zhang Shaojie, the leader of the corps, telegraphed Zhang Xueliang yesterday, saying, "Commander Zhang, Beiping, esteemed sir. Your reply has been received. Since you are reorganizing your troops and heading east, I hope you will be determined to fight the violent Japanese to the death. I am now leading hundreds of passionate youths north, vowing to be the vanguard. If you cannot depart, we will also decide to go to Heilongjiang Province, regardless of sacrifice, and must reach our destination. We hope for assistance at that time."

Corps Members Join

The corps members who joined yesterday included Zhou Kegong, who had originally joined the corps and sworn an oath with blood but was forced back by his family and escaped again, Wu Yuanyi, an overseas Chinese from Sumatra, a nurse from the Wusong Sanatorium (who did not want to announce her name for fear of family interference), and Shen Xunru from Haimen, totaling more than ten people.

Rear Support

The rear support consultants of the corps, Huang Jingwan, Zhang Yichen, Wu Shan, Tan Bozhi, Pan Xulun, and Qian Jianqiu, held a meeting at Yipinxiang last night to discuss the organization of the rear support group, methods for promoting the corps, and raising funds.

Corps Statement

In order to prevent villains from swindling under their name, the corps issued a statement to all circles, stating that after the corps goes north, there will be no corps members left behind to solicit donations. If enthusiastic compatriots provide assistance, they can send it directly to the Shanghai Bank in person and obtain a receipt. For the Nanyang area, please send it to the Hefeng Bank. In case of any swindling under their name, please immediately stop it.

Zhang Futian Successfully Immitates Building a Single-Wing Airplane 97

According to Huadong News Agency, Zhang Futian of this city's Automotive Editorial Office has recently immitated the building of an American single-wing light airplane and succeeded after five months of work. The details are as follows:

Immitation Process

At the end of May this year, when the aviation conference was held, Zhang Futian believed that the aviation industry was developing rapidly, but apart from the Navy Aircraft Manufacturing Department, there were no other successors in the country who built their own aircraft. Therefore, he decided to try building an aircraft himself. However, since large ones were too expensive, he decided to immitate the American single-wing light airplane (RusselHendersonMonoplane) and immediately started work. By the end of October, it was completed.

Aircraft Costs

The aircraft's engine is a Hunterson machine free car air-cooled engine, which Zhang bought for 30 yuan. The fabric of the fuselage is domestic coarse cloth. The paint and wood are also domestic products. However, the shrinkage force of domestic paint is weak and cannot withstand changes in the air. Therefore, the wings (the wings are made of British fine yarn, as domestic products cannot be used) had to be tightened three times before they could be completed, but they are still not comparable to foreign aircraft. The assistants to Zhang were a sofa chair tailor, an ordinary carpenter, and an ordinary automobile coppersmith. To check the horizontal and vertical planes, ordinary levels were used, as these components could not be purchased domestically. The total cost was 1,400 yuan, which is only one-sixtieth of the cost of purchasing an aircraft from abroad, which costs more than 70,000 yuan per aircraft. According to Zhang, the cost of the second successful aircraft can be further reduced.

Aircraft Details

The aircraft's horsepower is only 23 horsepower, with four cylinders, a speed of 70 miles per hour, and can fly 800 feet per minute. However, it can only seat one driver.

A Glimpse of the Fuselage

The fuselage is more than 15 feet long and 26 feet wide. The wings are yellow, as are the pillows and elevators. The sides of the nose are red, and the fuselage is green. It can store three gallons of fuel and can fly for three hours.

Application for Test Flight

After the aircraft was completed, Zhang applied to the China Aviation Corporation and aviation factories for a test flight, but was politely rejected by all parties. Therefore, he had to apply to the Aviation Administration for a test flight. The Aviation Administration has approved it, will send personnel to review it, and then schedule a test flight. They have also praised Zhang's imitation and have ordered him to report the cost.

Zhang's Brief Biography

Zhang is a native of Liuhe, Jiangsu, 36 years old, and graduated from the mechanical department of the American Wan Guo Correspondence School. He has worked in automobile and steamship engineering and has authored books such as Practical Automobile Repair and Working Methods and Practical Automobile Study with Repair Methods.

Cheng Zhenjun Returns to Beijing to Report on Negotiations

Still Coming to Shanghai to Prepare for Reception of Six Experts

Expressions of Patriotism from All Circles 100

A Telegram from Radio Station Employees to the Ministry of Transportation

All employees of the National Radio Station telegraphed the Central Government, saying, "Urgent, Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, National Government, esteemed sirs, the loss of the Eastern Provinces is nearly three months. Foreign insults are deepening, and national affairs are increasingly urgent. Our country did not prepare in advance and has no good policies after the fact. Diplomacy does not prioritize public opinion, and the military does not fulfill its duty to defend the territory. The Eastern Provinces were lost in the past due to non-resistance, and the humiliating treaty is about to be tacitly recognized in the future. The people are running and shouting, but the authorities are superficially accommodating. Students go to Beijing to petition, but are seen as being used. Thinking of this, where do our tears come from? We employees are deeply concerned about the difficulties of the times, as if sitting on pins and needles, looking ahead to the future, our hearts are filled with worry. As citizens, how can we sit idly by? Therefore, we telegraph and request that your ministry firmly reject the proposal to demarcate Jinzhou as a neutral zone, and firmly deny the proposal for joint administration of Tianjin. Immediately implement revolutionary diplomacy and recover lost territory by force to protect the country and defend national rights. All students arrested for petitioning should also be released immediately to comply with public opinion and safeguard human rights. The national situation is precarious, and the situation is dire. We are telegraphing with grief and anticipation. All employees of the National Radio Station under the Ministry of Transportation."

Resolutions of the Shanghai County Anti-Japanese Association

The Shanghai County Anti-Japanese Association held its seventh executive meeting at the County Party Headquarters yesterday afternoon. Six committee members, including Peng Liren, attended. Jiang Yanchiu presided, and Chen Guoan recorded. The meeting was held as scheduled. The important resolutions discussed were: (1) To telegraph the National Government to severely punish Gu Weijun, the Minister of Foreign Affairs, for his actions that harmed national sovereignty and humiliated the country. Resolution: Unanimously passed. (2) To telegraph the Fourth Central Committee to convene the First Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Committee as soon as possible and resolve the national crisis in accordance with the resolutions of the Peace Conference. Resolution: Passed. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

He lost Longjiang due to lack of support and exhausted supplies. How sad is this news! We have not heard of any troops from various places coming to support him. We hope you will immediately prepare to mobilize and go north to defeat the enemy. We will respectfully await the good news. As for the issue of supplies, please do not worry. Overseas Chinese from the Philippines Come to Shanghai to Join the Military 101

Fu Haishui, an overseas Chinese living in Merida, Leyte, Philippines, originally from Quanzhou, Fujian, has been running a grocery store in the Philippines and has two sons and four daughters. Recently, seeing the danger of the motherland's subjugation, he reads Chinese and Western newspapers every day, reporting the enthusiastic patriotic mood of the Chinese people in resisting Japan and saving the country. His patriotic heart was greatly moved. He specially ordered his eldest son, Fu Weikun, who is only twenty years old, to return to the motherland to participate in the anti-Japanese work, to fulfill the national duty of saving the country. Fu has already been ordered to come to Shanghai to join the military and went to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Volunteer Army Committee yesterday, requesting them to find a way to provide assistance so that he can fulfill his great wish to resist Japan and save the country. The Municipal Volunteer Army Committee has temporarily designated the Second District Citizen Association as Fu's temporary residence and plans to assign Fu to the First Battalion of the army for military training so that he can serve the country after completing his studies. It is also reported that Fu grew up overseas and is not good at Chinese, but he is fluent in English, so he can only be talked to and questioned in English.

The Banking Association Decides on Measures to Restrict the Export of Cash 102

Member Banks Certified by the Association

If Not a Member, Please Apply to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Regarding the issue of restricting the export of cash, after the Municipal Chamber of Commerce received telegrams from the Tianjin Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Silver and Money Guilds, suggesting that the Chamber of Commerce provide certification, the Chamber of Commerce sent letters to the local Banking and Money Trade Associations to solicit opinions. It is now heard that the Banking Association has decided that in the future, for members of the Association who transport cash for export to branches, agents, or affiliates of member banks, the Association will provide certification. If non-members need to transport cash for export, they should apply directly to the Chamber of Commerce for certification. The above measures have been officially replied to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce by the Banking Association for verification.

The Ministry of Railways Establishes the National Coal Transportation Committee 103

A Total of Twenty-Three Committee Members

Sixteen Million Tons Can Be Transported Monthly

The Ministry of Railways recently convened representatives from various relevant railways to a meeting to discuss concrete measures to relieve the coal shortage in Shanghai and the Yangtze River area. It is heard that as a result of the discussions, a National Coal Transportation Committee was officially established on the first of this month to be responsible for specifying the coal loading special trains on each railway and the loading and unloading of waterways. The committee has now stipulated the monthly transportation quantity of each railway. The Jinpu Railway will transport 60,000 tons to Pukou, the Pinghan Railway will transport 20,000 tons to Hankou, at least 30,000 tons of the coal exported through the Qingdao port via the Jiaoji Railway must be transported to Shanghai, the Beining Railway will allocate more carriages to Kailuan and other mines, transporting an additional 50,000 tons to the Qinhuangdao port for export to Shanghai. A total of 160,000 tons can be transported by each railway monthly. However, the coal must be transported to waterways and transferred by ships in order to reach Shanghai continuously. It is heard that the Ministry has consulted with the Ministry of Communications on joint transportation measures. The coal shortage in Shanghai and the Yangtze River area should be resolved. The National Coal Transportation Committee has a total of twenty-three members, all of whom are transportation experts selected and dispatched by the Ministry and railways. The names of the committee members are as follows: Chairman Qian Zongze, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Railways, Vice Chairman Guan Genglin, Director of the Business Department, and consultants Liu Jingshan, Yang Xianfen, Xiao Qizhan, Hu Jie, Huang Zhensheng, Xu Chuanyin, Shen Zhongyu, Huang Lint, Wu Shaozeng, Lu Shao'e, Lao Mian, Wang Tairui, Zhang You, Liang Yongzhang, Qian Zongyuan, Chen Yongqing, Yu Changfu, Qiu Hongxun, Zhou Songnian, Peng Dongyuan, and Tan Shukui.

Overseas Chinese from the Philippines Come to Shanghai to Join the Military 105

Fu Haishui, an overseas Chinese living in Merida, Leyte, Philippines, originally from Quanzhou, Fujian, has been running a grocery store in the Philippines and has two sons and four daughters. Recently, seeing the danger of the motherland's subjugation, he reads Chinese and Western newspapers every day, reporting the enthusiastic patriotic mood of the Chinese people in resisting Japan and saving the country. His patriotic heart was greatly moved. He specially ordered his eldest son, Fu Weikun, who is only twenty years old, to return to the motherland to participate in the anti-Japanese work, to fulfill the national duty of saving the country. Fu has already been ordered to come to Shanghai to join the military and went to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Volunteer Army Committee yesterday, requesting them to find a way to provide assistance so that he can fulfill his great wish to resist Japan and save the country. News on the Preparation of Air Main Lines 112

Trial Flight to Chengdu in Mid-Month

Aircraft for the Shanghai-Guangdong Line Ordered from the United States

The China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Chengdu main line has already opened to traffic and reached Chongqing. The preparation for flight and station establishment between Chongqing and Chengdu will be realized in the near future. The Shanghai-Guangdong line is also under preparation. The survey news of the main lines is recorded separately as follows:

Regarding the trial flight to Chengdu and station establishment in Chongqing and Chengdu, the company has repeatedly consulted with the Sichuan provincial authorities by telegram. Recently, it has obtained the approval of Liu Wenhui, chairman of Sichuan Province. The airport will be located near Phoenix Mountain in Chengdu, where the plains are vast and flat, which is very suitable for establishing a site. The radio required by the station has already been purchased in Shanghai and will be transported there soon. The Chongqing-Chengdu section trial flight will be carried out in mid-month. The aircraft will use the land aircraft of the Beijing-Ping main line, because the distance between them is very close, and the flight only takes two hours. The official opening of the route will be within two months.

Shanghai-Guangdong Route Preparation. The Shanghai-Guangdong line plans to set up stations along the coast, including Ningbo, Wenzhou, Xiamen, Fuzhou, Shantou, and Guangzhou. Each station will use the original equipment of the military and political departments to prepare for aircraft takeoff and landing. Because the aircraft on the Beijing-Ping and Shanghai-Hankou lines are not enough for allocation, the company officially sent a telegram to the American Commercial Transportation Company in New York yesterday, requesting the American aircraft factory to manufacture four seaplanes on its behalf. The speed of flight will be increased by 30 miles per hour (that is, 140 miles) compared with the aircraft currently in operation. These new aircraft will be transported to China in about three months. The Shanghai-Guangdong line is scheduled to be officially opened to traffic in April of the 21st year of the Republic of China.

Beijing-Ganzhou Route Uncertain. The preparation for the Beijing-Ganzhou route is difficult to realize for a while, because the commerce along the route is not very developed. Even if the Chongqing-Chengdu section and the Shanghai-Guangdong line are completed, the company's board of directors will still have to deliberate and consider the situation before making a decision.
